Because of Betty Bumpers‚Äô efforts, more than 95% of American children today are protected against once dreaded childhood diseases. Her accomplishments will continue to be an inspiration to everyone working in public health. We at CDC mourn the passing of this great American.

@ncnative46 Poliomyelitis is caused by poliovirus. CDC tests every stool specimen from reported AFM cases for poliovirus; all specimens we‚Äôve received tested negative. Because of high vaccination coverage against polio in the US &amp; globally, we no longer see cases of poliomyelitis in the US.
@RoseOfKali @CDCgov AFM is not a U.S.-specific issue and is well-documented in other countries across Europe, Canada, Japan, and Australia.  All stool specimens from AFM patients that CDC has received have tested negative for poliovirus.

CDC providing emergency response to DRC during the #Ebola outbreak as needed to enhance disease tracking, laboratory testing, and developing guidance and tools to conduct public health investigations and implementation of ring vaccination.
Tests shows the #Ebola virus species of current DRC outbreak is ebolavirus Zaire, but genetically different than the one that caused an outbreak earlier this year in another DRC province. Genetic testing of viruses can be critical to determine if outbreaks are linked or new.
CDC has deployed experienced #Ebola experts to DRC and the World Health Organization to provide guidance on coordination of outbreak response, laboratory testing, disease contact tracing, infection control, and health communication.
CDC has been responding and coordinating with the Ministry of Health of the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC) since a new outbreak of #Ebola in North Kivu province was reported on 7/30/2018. https://t.co/d1OIYJuHEk

Children 9 years and older are only recommended 1 dose of flu vaccine. For kids getting vaccinated the first time, protection only sets in after the second dose is given. So a child who needed two doses but did not get the second dose would not be considered fully vaccinated.
Fully vaccinated means the child has received the correct number of doses of #flu vaccine recommended for them. Children aged 6 months through 8 years getting vaccinated for the first time are recommended to get 2 doses of flu vaccine.

For people who are very sick with #flu ‚Äì or at high-risk of serious complications, such as children, the elderly, or pregnant women‚Äì we recommend prompt treatment with antiviral medications. This could mean the difference between a milder illness and a hospital stay or worse.
We recognize this #flu season has been hard on families and that we‚Äôve lost too many children because of flu. CDC continues to recommend parents get their kids vaccinated each year against the flu.
This season‚Äôs #flu vaccine offered better protection against H3N2 for children six months to eight years old, with an estimated effectiveness of 51%. Overall, flu vaccine was 59% effective against both influenza A and B in children.
Vaccine effectiveness against this season‚Äôs dominant H3N2 #flu viruses was about 25%. However, the vaccine was better at protecting against the other circulating flu viruses. For example, it provided 67% protection against H1N1 and 42% against influenza B viruses.
According to estimates, U.S. #flu vaccines were 36% effective overall against influenza A and B. That might not sound impressive, but it means a vaccinated person reduced risk of getting sick with the flu and having to go to the doctor by about one-third.

Watch for more severe #flu symptoms like persistent high fever, difficulty breathing or shortness of breath, or rapid heartbeat. Another severe symptom: you start to get better, then suddenly feel much worse. Seek medical attention immediately in this situation.
For those who are already sick, please stay home from work or school. Otherwise you run the risk of spreading #flu to others ‚Äì and what may be mild symptoms to you could be deadly to someone else.
We continue to recommend antiviral treatment for people who are very sick with #flu or people who are at high risk of serious flu complications who develop flu symptoms.
#Flu can make people more vulnerable to secondary infections like bacterial pneumonia, so we recommend people 65 and over get the pneumococcal pneumonia vaccine.
We continue to recommend getting the #flu vaccine to prevent flu. It‚Äôs true that flu vaccines often have lower effectiveness against H3N2 viruses. However, the vaccine‚Äôs effectiveness against other flu viruses is better. And some protection is better than none.
This #flu season continues to be particularly challenging. CDC‚Äôs latest tracking data indicate that flu activity is still on the rise overall. Influenza A H3N2 viruses continue to dominate this season, and are often linked to more severe illness.
